{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_013eXBZEhuUvPfm4Sq9qFhx3","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01E6d3dyyWm282PqCskR3psN","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/docs/gdscript_vm_reference.md","content":"# GDScript VM Bytecode Reference\n\nInternal developer documentation for the GDScript virtual machine bytecode instruction set.\n\n**Key source files:**\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_function.h` — opcode enum, address encoding, `GDScriptFunction`\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_vm.cpp` — interpreter dispatch loop and per-opcode execution logic\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_compiler.cpp` — AST-to-bytecode compilation\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_byte_codegen.h/.cpp` — low-level bytecode emitter\n\n---\n\n## VM Architecture\n\nThe GDScript VM is **register-based with a flat Variant array (\"stack\")**. It is not a push/pop stack machine; every instruction operand is an explicit address referencing a slot in one of three address spaces. The instruction pointer (`ip`) advances by a fixed number of words per instruction (the exact increment is hard-coded per opcode in the handler body).\n\n### Dispatch mechanism\n\nOn GCC/Clang the VM uses **computed goto** (`goto *switch_table_ops[opcode]`) for the inner dispatch loop, which avoids the branch-predictor miss of a `switch`. On MSVC a `switch` statement is used instead. Both paths are guarded by the macros `OPCODE_SWITCH`, `DISPATCH_OPCODE`, etc. defined in `gdscript_vm.cpp:371-404`.\n\n### Execution entry\n\nThe interpreter entry point is:\n\n```cpp\nVariant GDScriptFunction::call(\n    GDScriptInstance *p_instance,\n    const Variant **p_args, int p_argcount,\n    Callable::CallError &r_err,\n    CallState *p_state = nullptr);   // non-null when resuming after await\n```\n\n(`gdscript_vm.cpp:448`)\n\n---\n\n## Instruction Word Layout\n\nEach instruction occupies one or more 32-bit integers (`int`) in the `GDScriptFunction::code` array. The first word is always the opcode value (the enum constant). Subsequent words encode operand addresses, inline immediates, or pointers split across multiple words.\n\n### Operand address encoding\n\nEvery operand address is a single 32-bit word split into two fields (`gdscript_function.h:373-381`):\n\n```\n 31       24 23                    0\n ┌─────────┬───────────────────────┐\n │  type   │        index          │\n └─────────┴───────────────────────┘\n   ADDR_BITS = 24   ADDR_MASK = (1<<24)-1\n```\n\n| `type` bits | Meaning | Resolved array |\n|---|---|---|\n| `0` (`ADDR_TYPE_STACK`) | Local/parameter stack slot | `stack[]` (alloca'd per call) |\n| `1` (`ADDR_TYPE_CONSTANT`) | Compile-time constant pool | `_constants_ptr[]` |\n| `2` (`ADDR_TYPE_MEMBER`) | Instance member array | `p_instance->members[]` |\n\nThe macro `GET_VARIANT_PTR(name, code_offset)` (vm.cpp:617) decodes an address word at `_code_ptr[ip + 1 + code_offset]` and resolves it to a `Variant *`.\n\n### Fixed stack slots (indices 0–2)\n\nThree stack slots are reserved at every call frame (`gdscript_function.h:383-391`):\n\n| Index | Constant | Contents |\n|---|---|---|\n| 0 | `ADDR_STACK_SELF` | The `Object *` owner of the current instance (or `null` for static calls) |\n| 1 | `ADDR_STACK_CLASS` | The `GDScript *` class object |\n| 2 | `ADDR_STACK_NIL` | Always `null` / `Variant()` — used as a discard target |\n\nUser parameters start at stack index 3.\n\n### Instruction-argument block\n\nSeveral variable-arity instructions (calls, constructs, iterates) prepend an argument-count word and then N address words before the fixed operands. The macro `LOAD_INSTRUCTION_ARGS` (vm.cpp:655) reads this block into a side array `instruction_args[]`, then advances `ip` by `instr_arg_count + 1` so the fixed operands follow at known offsets.\n\n---\n\n## Opcode Table\n\nOpcodes are defined in `GDScriptFunction::Opcode` (`gdscript_function.h:218-371`).\n\n### Arithmetic & Logic\n\n| Opcode | Words (total) | Operands | Notes |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_OPERATOR` | 7 + ptr_words | `a`, `b`, `dst`, op_enum, signature_cache, ret_type_cache, func_ptr_cache | Polymorphic; caches validated evaluator on first run |\n| `OPCODE_OPERATOR_VALIDATED` | 5 | `a`, `b`, `dst`, func_idx | Pre-validated fast path; `func_idx` indexes `_operator_funcs_ptr[]` |\n\n`OPCODE_OPERATOR` layout (vm.cpp:691):\n```\n[opcode][addr_a][addr_b][addr_dst][op_enum][sig_cache][ret_type_cache][func_ptr…]\n```\n\n### Type Tests (`is` operator)\n\n| Opcode | Words | Operands |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_BUILTIN` | 4 | `dst`, `value`, builtin_type_int |\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_ARRAY` | 6 | `dst`, `value`, `script_type`, builtin_type_int, native_name_idx |\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_NATIVE` | 4 | `dst`, `value`, native_name_idx |\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_SCRIPT` | 4 | `dst`, `value`, `type` (addr of Script object) |\n\nResult is a `bool` written to `dst`.\n\n### Property / Key Access\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_SET_KEYED` | 4 | `dst[index] = value` — generic, uses `Variant::set()` |\n| `OPCODE_SET_KEYED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Same + keyed_setter_idx into `_keyed_setters_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_SET_INDEXED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Integer-index fast path; setter_idx → `_indexed_setters_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_KEYED` | 4 | `dst = src[index]` — generic |\n| `OPCODE_GET_KEYED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Fast keyed getter |\n| `OPCODE_GET_INDEXED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Fast integer-index getter |\n| `OPCODE_SET_NAMED` | 4 | `dst.name = value`; name_idx → `_global_names_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_SET_NAMED_VALIDATED` | 4 | Fast; setter_idx → `_setters_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_NAMED` | 4 | `dst = src.name` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_NAMED_VALIDATED` | 4 | Fast; getter_idx → `_getters_ptr[]` |\n\n### Member Variable Access (GDScript instance properties)\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_SET_MEMBER` | 3 | `ClassDB::set_property(owner, name, src)` — sets engine property |\n| `OPCODE_GET_MEMBER` | 3 | `ClassDB::get_property(owner, name, dst)` — gets engine property |\n| `OPCODE_SET_STATIC_VARIABLE` | 4 | `gdscript->static_variables[index] = value` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_STATIC_VARIABLE` | 4 | `target = gdscript->static_variables[index]` |\n\n`OPCODE_SET_MEMBER` / `OPCODE_GET_MEMBER` go through the engine property system (`ClassDB`), not through the GDScript member array. GDScript instance variables declared with `var` are stored in `p_instance->members[]` and accessed via `ADDR_TYPE_MEMBER` addressing in normal operands, **not** through these opcodes.\n\n### Assignment\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN` | 3 | `dst = src` (Variant copy) |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_NULL` | 2 | `dst = null` |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TRUE` | 2 | `dst = true` |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_FALSE` | 2 | `dst = false` |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_BUILTIN` | 4 | Typed assign with implicit conversion to builtin_type |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_ARRAY` | varies | Typed array assign with element type metadata |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_NATIVE` | 4 | Typed assign for native class, with null-check |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_SCRIPT` | 4 | Typed assign for Script subclass |\n\n### Type Casts\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CAST_TO_BUILTIN` | Explicit cast to a builtin Variant type |\n| `OPCODE_CAST_TO_NATIVE` | Explicit cast to a native engine class |\n| `OPCODE_CAST_TO_SCRIPT` | Explicit cast to a GDScript class |\n\n### Construction\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT` | `Type(arg0, …)` for builtin types — uses `Variant::construct()` |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_VALIDATED` | Same, pre-looked-up constructor; idx → `_constructors_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_ARRAY` | `[a, b, c]` array literal |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_TYPED_ARRAY` | `Array[T](…)` typed array literal |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_DICTIONARY` | `{k:v, …}` dictionary literal; args interleaved key/value |\n\n`OPCODE_CONSTRUCT` layout (vm.cpp:1580):\n```\n[opcode][argc_word (instr-arg block)] … [argc][builtin_type_int][dst addr]\n```\n\n### Function Calls\n\nAll call opcodes share a common pattern for variable-arity arguments: a `LOAD_INSTRUCTION_ARGS` block precedes the fixed operands.\n\n#### Dynamic dispatch (`OPCODE_CALL`, `OPCODE_CALL_RETURN`, `OPCODE_CALL_ASYNC`)\n\nUsed when the method is called on a Variant (possibly unknown type at compile time).\n\n```\n[opcode]\n  [N]          ← LOAD_INSTRUCTION_ARGS: arg count word\n  [addr_arg0] … [addr_argN-1]\n  [addr_base]  ← instruction_args[argc]\n  [argc]       ← _code_ptr[ip+1] after advancing ip by instr_arg_count\n  [name_idx]   ← index into _global_names_ptr[]\n  [addr_ret]   ← instruction_args[argc+1] (only CALL_RETURN / CALL_ASYNC)\n```\n\n- `OPCODE_CALL`: no return value captured (result discarded)\n- `OPCODE_CALL_RETURN`: return value written to `addr_ret`\n- `OPCODE_CALL_ASYNC`: like `CALL_RETURN` but allows returning a `GDScriptFunctionState`\n\n#### Pre-bound method calls\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND` | Calls a `MethodBind *` on an Object; no return captured |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND_RET` | Same, return captured |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND_VALIDATED_RETURN` | Uses `method->validated_call()`; return captured |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND_VALIDATED_NO_RETURN` | Uses `method->validated_call()`; no return |\n\n`MethodBind *` is resolved by index into `_methods_ptr[]` (vm.cpp:1845).\n\n#### Static calls\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CALL_BUILTIN_STATIC` | `Variant::call_static(type, name, …)` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_NATIVE_STATIC` | Static native method via `MethodBind` (`instance = nullptr`) |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_NATIVE_STATIC_VALIDATED_RETURN` | Same, validated path, return |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_NATIVE_STATIC_VALIDATED_NO_RETURN` | Same, no return |\n\n#### Utility & GDScript built-ins\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CALL_UTILITY` | `Variant::call_utility_function(name, …)` — engine utility (e.g., `print`) |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_UTILITY_VALIDATED` | Validated utility; idx → `_utilities_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_GDSCRIPT_UTILITY` | GDScript-specific utilities (e.g., `str`, `inst_to_dict`); idx → `_gds_utilities_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_BUILTIN_TYPE_VALIDATED` | Validated call on a builtin-type method; idx → `_builtin_methods_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_SELF_BASE` | Calls an overridden base-class method (super); walks `_script->base` chain |\n\n### Async / Coroutines\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_AWAIT` | 4 | Suspends execution; serializes stack into a `GDScriptFunctionState`; connects to signal |\n| `OPCODE_AWAIT_RESUME` | 2 | Placed immediately after `OPCODE_AWAIT`; restores result on resume |\n\nWhen `OPCODE_AWAIT` receives a non-signal value it falls through synchronously, jumping over `OPCODE_AWAIT_RESUME` (vm.cpp:2380-2383).\n\n### Lambda Creation\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CREATE_LAMBDA` | Creates a `Callable` from a nested `GDScriptFunction`; captures N variables |\n| `OPCODE_CREATE_SELF_LAMBDA` | Same, but binds the current `self` as the callable's owner |\n\nCaptured variables are passed as instruction arguments. The lambda's `GDScriptFunction *` is resolved by index into `_lambdas_ptr[]`.\n\n### Control Flow\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_JUMP` | 2 | Unconditional jump; `ip = _code_ptr[ip+1]` |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_IF` | 3 | Jump if `test.booleanize() == true` |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_IF_NOT` | 3 | Jump if `test.booleanize() == false` |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_TO_DEF_ARGUMENT` | 2 | Jump to handler for the next missing default argument |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_IF_SHARED` | 3 | Jump if value is a shared (reference) type — used for copy-on-write |\n\nAll jump targets are absolute code array indices.\n\n### Return\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_RETURN` | 2 | `retvalue = *r`; exit interpreter loop |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_BUILTIN` | 3 | Return with implicit conversion to builtin_type |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_ARRAY` | varies | Return typed array with element-type validation |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_NATIVE` | 3 | Return with native-class type check |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_SCRIPT` | 3 | Return with Script-subclass type check |\n\n### Iteration (`for` loops)\n\nThe `for x in collection` construct compiles to a pair of opcodes:\n\n1. **`OPCODE_ITERATE_BEGIN_*`** — Initialises iteration state; jumps to after-loop on empty.\n2. **`OPCODE_ITERATE_*`** — Advances to next element; jumps to after-loop when exhausted.\n\nSpecialised variants exist for every iterable Variant type to avoid virtual dispatch:\n\n`INT`, `FLOAT`, `VECTOR2`, `VECTOR2I`, `VECTOR3`, `VECTOR3I`, `STRING`, `DICTIONARY`, `ARRAY`, `PACKED_BYTE_ARRAY`, `PACKED_INT32_ARRAY`, `PACKED_INT64_ARRAY`, `PACKED_FLOAT32_ARRAY`, `PACKED_FLOAT64_ARRAY`, `PACKED_STRING_ARRAY`, `PACKED_VECTOR2_ARRAY`, `PACKED_VECTOR3_ARRAY`, `PACKED_COLOR_ARRAY`, `PACKED_VECTOR4_ARRAY`, `OBJECT`\n\nThe generic `OPCODE_ITERATE_BEGIN` / `OPCODE_ITERATE` (without a type suffix) uses runtime dispatch.\n\n### Global / Named Global Storage\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_STORE_GLOBAL` | Copy a global singleton into a stack slot |\n| `OPCODE_STORE_NAMED_GLOBAL` | Copy a named global (e.g., `Engine`, `OS`) into a stack slot |\n\n### Type Adjust\n\n`OPCODE_TYPE_ADJUST_<TYPE>` — reinitialises a stack slot to the correct in-memory layout for a specific Variant type without changing its value. Used after assignments to typed temporaries to ensure the internal Variant tag and data are consistent.\n\nOne variant exists per concrete Variant type (bool, int, float, String, Vector2, …, PackedVector4Array).\n\n### Debug / Meta\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_ASSERT` | Evaluates a condition; prints message and aborts in debug builds |\n| `OPCODE_BREAKPOINT` | Triggers the engine debugger breakpoint |\n| `OPCODE_LINE` | Records the current source line number for stack traces / debugger |\n| `OPCODE_END` | Sentinel — marks the end of valid opcodes (also used as array-size assert) |\n\n---\n\n## Function Call Convention\n\n### Argument passing\n\nArguments are passed **by value** as `Variant` copies placed directly onto the callee's stack. At call setup (vm.cpp:534):\n\n1. The caller passes a `const Variant **p_args` array and a count.\n2. For each argument: if the parameter has a declared type and the argument already matches, the Variant is copied directly (`memnew_placement`). If an implicit conversion is needed and allowed, `Variant::construct()` is called. Type errors produce `CALL_ERROR_INVALID_ARGUMENT`.\n3. Arguments land at stack indices **3, 4, 5, …** (after the three fixed slots).\n4. Remaining stack slots (temporaries, locals without initial args) are zero-initialised with `memnew_placement(&stack[i], Variant)`.\n\n### Default arguments\n\nIf fewer arguments than parameters are supplied, `defarg = _argument_count - p_argcount` is set. The `OPCODE_JUMP_TO_DEF_ARGUMENT` opcode jumps to `_default_arg_ptr[defarg]`, which is a code offset where the default-value assignment is compiled.\n\n### Return value\n\nThe callee writes its return value to a local `Variant retvalue` and that is returned from `GDScriptFunction::call()` by value. The caller optionally stores it via an `addr_ret` operand.\n\n### Call depth limit\n\nA thread-local counter `call_depth` is incremented on entry and decremented on exit. The limit is `MAX_CALL_DEPTH = 2048` (gdscript_function.h:516). Exceeding it produces a \"Stack overflow\" error without crashing.\n\n---\n\n## Local Variable and Member Variable Access\n\n### Local variables & parameters\n\nStored in the per-call `stack[]` array allocated with `alloca()`. Accessed via `ADDR_TYPE_STACK` addresses. The compiler (`GDScriptByteCodeGenerator`) assigns each named local a fixed stack index that persists for the lifetime of its scope.\n\n### GDScript instance variables (`var x`)\n\nStored in `GDScriptInstance::members` (a `Vector<Variant>`). Accessed directly via `ADDR_TYPE_MEMBER` address words — the upper bits encode type=2, the lower 24 bits are the member index. No opcode is needed beyond the address encoding itself.\n\n### Engine properties (exported / native properties)\n\nAccessed via `OPCODE_SET_MEMBER` / `OPCODE_GET_MEMBER`, which route through `ClassDB::set_property` / `ClassDB::get_property`. These are used for properties defined by the engine's native class hierarchy, not for GDScript `var` declarations.\n\n### Constants\n\nStored in `GDScriptFunction::constants` and accessed via `ADDR_TYPE_CONSTANT` addresses. Includes literal values compiled into the function, as well as pre-computed `StringName` keys used by property-access opcodes.\n\n### Static variables\n\nStored in `GDScript::static_variables` (a `Vector<Variant>` on the class object). Accessed via `OPCODE_GET_STATIC_VARIABLE` / `OPCODE_SET_STATIC_VARIABLE`, which resolve the target class from a stack slot holding the `GDScript *` object, then index into `static_variables` by an integer operand.\n\n---\n\n## Type System Interaction\n\nAll values in the VM are `Variant` instances (24 bytes each on 64-bit). The `Variant::Type` enum (28 concrete types) determines the active union member. The VM uses typed fast paths when the compiler can prove the type at compile time:\n\n- **Validated operators/getters/setters/constructors/methods**: function pointers looked up once and stored in per-function pointer arrays (`_operator_funcs_ptr`, `_setters_ptr`, `_getters_ptr`, `_builtin_methods_ptr`, `_constructors_ptr`). The opcode encodes an index into the appropriate array.\n- **Type-adjust opcodes**: `OPCODE_TYPE_ADJUST_<T>` ensures the internal Variant tag matches the declared slot type, allowing validated calls to bypass tag checks.\n- **`OPCODE_OPERATOR` signature caching**: On first execution the operand types are observed and the validated evaluator is stored inline in the code array. Subsequent executions with the same types use the cached path (vm.cpp:715-773).\n\n`GDScriptDataType` (`gdscript_function.h:47`) is the compile-time type descriptor used by the compiler. At runtime, type checks use `Variant::get_type()`, `ClassDB::is_parent_class()`, and script inheritance walks.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5970,"cache_read_input_tokens":56253,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":5970,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"62edbcf1-a042-4dc3-8ac9-5562a8eb8926","uuid":"594c572b-d6be-4924-aa06-2ec1491c85f3"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01E6d3dyyWm282PqCskR3psN","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/docs/gdscript_vm_reference.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"62edbcf1-a042-4dc3-8ac9-5562a8eb8926","uuid":"51482ccc-69b8-4287-b5a7-f47332e5cc25","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/docs/gdscript_vm_reference.md","content":"# GDScript VM Bytecode Reference\n\nInternal developer documentation for the GDScript virtual machine bytecode instruction set.\n\n**Key source files:**\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_function.h` — opcode enum, address encoding, `GDScriptFunction`\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_vm.cpp` — interpreter dispatch loop and per-opcode execution logic\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_compiler.cpp` — AST-to-bytecode compilation\n- `modules/gdscript/gdscript_byte_codegen.h/.cpp` — low-level bytecode emitter\n\n---\n\n## VM Architecture\n\nThe GDScript VM is **register-based with a flat Variant array (\"stack\")**. It is not a push/pop stack machine; every instruction operand is an explicit address referencing a slot in one of three address spaces. The instruction pointer (`ip`) advances by a fixed number of words per instruction (the exact increment is hard-coded per opcode in the handler body).\n\n### Dispatch mechanism\n\nOn GCC/Clang the VM uses **computed goto** (`goto *switch_table_ops[opcode]`) for the inner dispatch loop, which avoids the branch-predictor miss of a `switch`. On MSVC a `switch` statement is used instead. Both paths are guarded by the macros `OPCODE_SWITCH`, `DISPATCH_OPCODE`, etc. defined in `gdscript_vm.cpp:371-404`.\n\n### Execution entry\n\nThe interpreter entry point is:\n\n```cpp\nVariant GDScriptFunction::call(\n    GDScriptInstance *p_instance,\n    const Variant **p_args, int p_argcount,\n    Callable::CallError &r_err,\n    CallState *p_state = nullptr);   // non-null when resuming after await\n```\n\n(`gdscript_vm.cpp:448`)\n\n---\n\n## Instruction Word Layout\n\nEach instruction occupies one or more 32-bit integers (`int`) in the `GDScriptFunction::code` array. The first word is always the opcode value (the enum constant). Subsequent words encode operand addresses, inline immediates, or pointers split across multiple words.\n\n### Operand address encoding\n\nEvery operand address is a single 32-bit word split into two fields (`gdscript_function.h:373-381`):\n\n```\n 31       24 23                    0\n ┌─────────┬───────────────────────┐\n │  type   │        index          │\n └─────────┴───────────────────────┘\n   ADDR_BITS = 24   ADDR_MASK = (1<<24)-1\n```\n\n| `type` bits | Meaning | Resolved array |\n|---|---|---|\n| `0` (`ADDR_TYPE_STACK`) | Local/parameter stack slot | `stack[]` (alloca'd per call) |\n| `1` (`ADDR_TYPE_CONSTANT`) | Compile-time constant pool | `_constants_ptr[]` |\n| `2` (`ADDR_TYPE_MEMBER`) | Instance member array | `p_instance->members[]` |\n\nThe macro `GET_VARIANT_PTR(name, code_offset)` (vm.cpp:617) decodes an address word at `_code_ptr[ip + 1 + code_offset]` and resolves it to a `Variant *`.\n\n### Fixed stack slots (indices 0–2)\n\nThree stack slots are reserved at every call frame (`gdscript_function.h:383-391`):\n\n| Index | Constant | Contents |\n|---|---|---|\n| 0 | `ADDR_STACK_SELF` | The `Object *` owner of the current instance (or `null` for static calls) |\n| 1 | `ADDR_STACK_CLASS` | The `GDScript *` class object |\n| 2 | `ADDR_STACK_NIL` | Always `null` / `Variant()` — used as a discard target |\n\nUser parameters start at stack index 3.\n\n### Instruction-argument block\n\nSeveral variable-arity instructions (calls, constructs, iterates) prepend an argument-count word and then N address words before the fixed operands. The macro `LOAD_INSTRUCTION_ARGS` (vm.cpp:655) reads this block into a side array `instruction_args[]`, then advances `ip` by `instr_arg_count + 1` so the fixed operands follow at known offsets.\n\n---\n\n## Opcode Table\n\nOpcodes are defined in `GDScriptFunction::Opcode` (`gdscript_function.h:218-371`).\n\n### Arithmetic & Logic\n\n| Opcode | Words (total) | Operands | Notes |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_OPERATOR` | 7 + ptr_words | `a`, `b`, `dst`, op_enum, signature_cache, ret_type_cache, func_ptr_cache | Polymorphic; caches validated evaluator on first run |\n| `OPCODE_OPERATOR_VALIDATED` | 5 | `a`, `b`, `dst`, func_idx | Pre-validated fast path; `func_idx` indexes `_operator_funcs_ptr[]` |\n\n`OPCODE_OPERATOR` layout (vm.cpp:691):\n```\n[opcode][addr_a][addr_b][addr_dst][op_enum][sig_cache][ret_type_cache][func_ptr…]\n```\n\n### Type Tests (`is` operator)\n\n| Opcode | Words | Operands |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_BUILTIN` | 4 | `dst`, `value`, builtin_type_int |\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_ARRAY` | 6 | `dst`, `value`, `script_type`, builtin_type_int, native_name_idx |\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_NATIVE` | 4 | `dst`, `value`, native_name_idx |\n| `OPCODE_TYPE_TEST_SCRIPT` | 4 | `dst`, `value`, `type` (addr of Script object) |\n\nResult is a `bool` written to `dst`.\n\n### Property / Key Access\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_SET_KEYED` | 4 | `dst[index] = value` — generic, uses `Variant::set()` |\n| `OPCODE_SET_KEYED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Same + keyed_setter_idx into `_keyed_setters_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_SET_INDEXED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Integer-index fast path; setter_idx → `_indexed_setters_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_KEYED` | 4 | `dst = src[index]` — generic |\n| `OPCODE_GET_KEYED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Fast keyed getter |\n| `OPCODE_GET_INDEXED_VALIDATED` | 5 | Fast integer-index getter |\n| `OPCODE_SET_NAMED` | 4 | `dst.name = value`; name_idx → `_global_names_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_SET_NAMED_VALIDATED` | 4 | Fast; setter_idx → `_setters_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_NAMED` | 4 | `dst = src.name` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_NAMED_VALIDATED` | 4 | Fast; getter_idx → `_getters_ptr[]` |\n\n### Member Variable Access (GDScript instance properties)\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_SET_MEMBER` | 3 | `ClassDB::set_property(owner, name, src)` — sets engine property |\n| `OPCODE_GET_MEMBER` | 3 | `ClassDB::get_property(owner, name, dst)` — gets engine property |\n| `OPCODE_SET_STATIC_VARIABLE` | 4 | `gdscript->static_variables[index] = value` |\n| `OPCODE_GET_STATIC_VARIABLE` | 4 | `target = gdscript->static_variables[index]` |\n\n`OPCODE_SET_MEMBER` / `OPCODE_GET_MEMBER` go through the engine property system (`ClassDB`), not through the GDScript member array. GDScript instance variables declared with `var` are stored in `p_instance->members[]` and accessed via `ADDR_TYPE_MEMBER` addressing in normal operands, **not** through these opcodes.\n\n### Assignment\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN` | 3 | `dst = src` (Variant copy) |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_NULL` | 2 | `dst = null` |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TRUE` | 2 | `dst = true` |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_FALSE` | 2 | `dst = false` |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_BUILTIN` | 4 | Typed assign with implicit conversion to builtin_type |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_ARRAY` | varies | Typed array assign with element type metadata |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_NATIVE` | 4 | Typed assign for native class, with null-check |\n| `OPCODE_ASSIGN_TYPED_SCRIPT` | 4 | Typed assign for Script subclass |\n\n### Type Casts\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CAST_TO_BUILTIN` | Explicit cast to a builtin Variant type |\n| `OPCODE_CAST_TO_NATIVE` | Explicit cast to a native engine class |\n| `OPCODE_CAST_TO_SCRIPT` | Explicit cast to a GDScript class |\n\n### Construction\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT` | `Type(arg0, …)` for builtin types — uses `Variant::construct()` |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_VALIDATED` | Same, pre-looked-up constructor; idx → `_constructors_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_ARRAY` | `[a, b, c]` array literal |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_TYPED_ARRAY` | `Array[T](…)` typed array literal |\n| `OPCODE_CONSTRUCT_DICTIONARY` | `{k:v, …}` dictionary literal; args interleaved key/value |\n\n`OPCODE_CONSTRUCT` layout (vm.cpp:1580):\n```\n[opcode][argc_word (instr-arg block)] … [argc][builtin_type_int][dst addr]\n```\n\n### Function Calls\n\nAll call opcodes share a common pattern for variable-arity arguments: a `LOAD_INSTRUCTION_ARGS` block precedes the fixed operands.\n\n#### Dynamic dispatch (`OPCODE_CALL`, `OPCODE_CALL_RETURN`, `OPCODE_CALL_ASYNC`)\n\nUsed when the method is called on a Variant (possibly unknown type at compile time).\n\n```\n[opcode]\n  [N]          ← LOAD_INSTRUCTION_ARGS: arg count word\n  [addr_arg0] … [addr_argN-1]\n  [addr_base]  ← instruction_args[argc]\n  [argc]       ← _code_ptr[ip+1] after advancing ip by instr_arg_count\n  [name_idx]   ← index into _global_names_ptr[]\n  [addr_ret]   ← instruction_args[argc+1] (only CALL_RETURN / CALL_ASYNC)\n```\n\n- `OPCODE_CALL`: no return value captured (result discarded)\n- `OPCODE_CALL_RETURN`: return value written to `addr_ret`\n- `OPCODE_CALL_ASYNC`: like `CALL_RETURN` but allows returning a `GDScriptFunctionState`\n\n#### Pre-bound method calls\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND` | Calls a `MethodBind *` on an Object; no return captured |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND_RET` | Same, return captured |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND_VALIDATED_RETURN` | Uses `method->validated_call()`; return captured |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_METHOD_BIND_VALIDATED_NO_RETURN` | Uses `method->validated_call()`; no return |\n\n`MethodBind *` is resolved by index into `_methods_ptr[]` (vm.cpp:1845).\n\n#### Static calls\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CALL_BUILTIN_STATIC` | `Variant::call_static(type, name, …)` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_NATIVE_STATIC` | Static native method via `MethodBind` (`instance = nullptr`) |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_NATIVE_STATIC_VALIDATED_RETURN` | Same, validated path, return |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_NATIVE_STATIC_VALIDATED_NO_RETURN` | Same, no return |\n\n#### Utility & GDScript built-ins\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CALL_UTILITY` | `Variant::call_utility_function(name, …)` — engine utility (e.g., `print`) |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_UTILITY_VALIDATED` | Validated utility; idx → `_utilities_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_GDSCRIPT_UTILITY` | GDScript-specific utilities (e.g., `str`, `inst_to_dict`); idx → `_gds_utilities_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_BUILTIN_TYPE_VALIDATED` | Validated call on a builtin-type method; idx → `_builtin_methods_ptr[]` |\n| `OPCODE_CALL_SELF_BASE` | Calls an overridden base-class method (super); walks `_script->base` chain |\n\n### Async / Coroutines\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_AWAIT` | 4 | Suspends execution; serializes stack into a `GDScriptFunctionState`; connects to signal |\n| `OPCODE_AWAIT_RESUME` | 2 | Placed immediately after `OPCODE_AWAIT`; restores result on resume |\n\nWhen `OPCODE_AWAIT` receives a non-signal value it falls through synchronously, jumping over `OPCODE_AWAIT_RESUME` (vm.cpp:2380-2383).\n\n### Lambda Creation\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_CREATE_LAMBDA` | Creates a `Callable` from a nested `GDScriptFunction`; captures N variables |\n| `OPCODE_CREATE_SELF_LAMBDA` | Same, but binds the current `self` as the callable's owner |\n\nCaptured variables are passed as instruction arguments. The lambda's `GDScriptFunction *` is resolved by index into `_lambdas_ptr[]`.\n\n### Control Flow\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_JUMP` | 2 | Unconditional jump; `ip = _code_ptr[ip+1]` |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_IF` | 3 | Jump if `test.booleanize() == true` |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_IF_NOT` | 3 | Jump if `test.booleanize() == false` |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_TO_DEF_ARGUMENT` | 2 | Jump to handler for the next missing default argument |\n| `OPCODE_JUMP_IF_SHARED` | 3 | Jump if value is a shared (reference) type — used for copy-on-write |\n\nAll jump targets are absolute code array indices.\n\n### Return\n\n| Opcode | Words | Description |\n|---|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_RETURN` | 2 | `retvalue = *r`; exit interpreter loop |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_BUILTIN` | 3 | Return with implicit conversion to builtin_type |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_ARRAY` | varies | Return typed array with element-type validation |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_NATIVE` | 3 | Return with native-class type check |\n| `OPCODE_RETURN_TYPED_SCRIPT` | 3 | Return with Script-subclass type check |\n\n### Iteration (`for` loops)\n\nThe `for x in collection` construct compiles to a pair of opcodes:\n\n1. **`OPCODE_ITERATE_BEGIN_*`** — Initialises iteration state; jumps to after-loop on empty.\n2. **`OPCODE_ITERATE_*`** — Advances to next element; jumps to after-loop when exhausted.\n\nSpecialised variants exist for every iterable Variant type to avoid virtual dispatch:\n\n`INT`, `FLOAT`, `VECTOR2`, `VECTOR2I`, `VECTOR3`, `VECTOR3I`, `STRING`, `DICTIONARY`, `ARRAY`, `PACKED_BYTE_ARRAY`, `PACKED_INT32_ARRAY`, `PACKED_INT64_ARRAY`, `PACKED_FLOAT32_ARRAY`, `PACKED_FLOAT64_ARRAY`, `PACKED_STRING_ARRAY`, `PACKED_VECTOR2_ARRAY`, `PACKED_VECTOR3_ARRAY`, `PACKED_COLOR_ARRAY`, `PACKED_VECTOR4_ARRAY`, `OBJECT`\n\nThe generic `OPCODE_ITERATE_BEGIN` / `OPCODE_ITERATE` (without a type suffix) uses runtime dispatch.\n\n### Global / Named Global Storage\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_STORE_GLOBAL` | Copy a global singleton into a stack slot |\n| `OPCODE_STORE_NAMED_GLOBAL` | Copy a named global (e.g., `Engine`, `OS`) into a stack slot |\n\n### Type Adjust\n\n`OPCODE_TYPE_ADJUST_<TYPE>` — reinitialises a stack slot to the correct in-memory layout for a specific Variant type without changing its value. Used after assignments to typed temporaries to ensure the internal Variant tag and data are consistent.\n\nOne variant exists per concrete Variant type (bool, int, float, String, Vector2, …, PackedVector4Array).\n\n### Debug / Meta\n\n| Opcode | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `OPCODE_ASSERT` | Evaluates a condition; prints message and aborts in debug builds |\n| `OPCODE_BREAKPOINT` | Triggers the engine debugger breakpoint |\n| `OPCODE_LINE` | Records the current source line number for stack traces / debugger |\n| `OPCODE_END` | Sentinel — marks the end of valid opcodes (also used as array-size assert) |\n\n---\n\n## Function Call Convention\n\n### Argument passing\n\nArguments are passed **by value** as `Variant` copies placed directly onto the callee's stack. At call setup (vm.cpp:534):\n\n1. The caller passes a `const Variant **p_args` array and a count.\n2. For each argument: if the parameter has a declared type and the argument already matches, the Variant is copied directly (`memnew_placement`). If an implicit conversion is needed and allowed, `Variant::construct()` is called. Type errors produce `CALL_ERROR_INVALID_ARGUMENT`.\n3. Arguments land at stack indices **3, 4, 5, …** (after the three fixed slots).\n4. Remaining stack slots (temporaries, locals without initial args) are zero-initialised with `memnew_placement(&stack[i], Variant)`.\n\n### Default arguments\n\nIf fewer arguments than parameters are supplied, `defarg = _argument_count - p_argcount` is set. The `OPCODE_JUMP_TO_DEF_ARGUMENT` opcode jumps to `_default_arg_ptr[defarg]`, which is a code offset where the default-value assignment is compiled.\n\n### Return value\n\nThe callee writes its return value to a local `Variant retvalue` and that is returned from `GDScriptFunction::call()` by value. The caller optionally stores it via an `addr_ret` operand.\n\n### Call depth limit\n\nA thread-local counter `call_depth` is incremented on entry and decremented on exit. The limit is `MAX_CALL_DEPTH = 2048` (gdscript_function.h:516). Exceeding it produces a \"Stack overflow\" error without crashing.\n\n---\n\n## Local Variable and Member Variable Access\n\n### Local variables & parameters\n\nStored in the per-call `stack[]` array allocated with `alloca()`. Accessed via `ADDR_TYPE_STACK` addresses. The compiler (`GDScriptByteCodeGenerator`) assigns each named local a fixed stack index that persists for the lifetime of its scope.\n\n### GDScript instance variables (`var x`)\n\nStored in `GDScriptInstance::members` (a `Vector<Variant>`). Accessed directly via `ADDR_TYPE_MEMBER` address words — the upper bits encode type=2, the lower 24 bits are the member index. No opcode is needed beyond the address encoding itself.\n\n### Engine properties (exported / native properties)\n\nAccessed via `OPCODE_SET_MEMBER` / `OPCODE_GET_MEMBER`, which route through `ClassDB::set_property` / `ClassDB::get_property`. These are used for properties defined by the engine's native class hierarchy, not for GDScript `var` declarations.\n\n### Constants\n\nStored in `GDScriptFunction::constants` and accessed via `ADDR_TYPE_CONSTANT` addresses. Includes literal values compiled into the function, as well as pre-computed `StringName` keys used by property-access opcodes.\n\n### Static variables\n\nStored in `GDScript::static_variables` (a `Vector<Variant>` on the class object). Accessed via `OPCODE_GET_STATIC_VARIABLE` / `OPCODE_SET_STATIC_VARIABLE`, which resolve the target class from a stack slot holding the `GDScript *` object, then index into `static_variables` by an integer operand.\n\n---\n\n## Type System Interaction\n\nAll values in the VM are `Variant` instances (24 bytes each on 64-bit). The `Variant::Type` enum (28 concrete types) determines the active union member. The VM uses typed fast paths when the compiler can prove the type at compile time:\n\n- **Validated operators/getters/setters/constructors/methods**: function pointers looked up once and stored in per-function pointer arrays (`_operator_funcs_ptr`, `_setters_ptr`, `_getters_ptr`, `_builtin_methods_ptr`, `_constructors_ptr`). The opcode encodes an index into the appropriate array.\n- **Type-adjust opcodes**: `OPCODE_TYPE_ADJUST_<T>` ensures the internal Variant tag matches the declared slot type, allowing validated calls to bypass tag checks.\n- **`OPCODE_OPERATOR` signature caching**: On first execution the operand types are observed and the validated evaluator is stored inline in the code array. Subsequent executions with the same types use the cached path (vm.cpp:715-773).\n\n`GDScriptDataType` (`gdscript_function.h:47`) is the compile-time type descriptor used by the compiler. At runtime, type checks use `Variant::get_type()`, `ClassDB::is_parent_class()`, and script inheritance walks.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
